Such accessibility includes the ability to execute, query, read to or write from the software component, as warranted.","The components of two exemplary systems in accordance with the present invention have been described in . Attention now turns to three use case scenarios that illustrate many of the advantages of the present invention. In the first use case scenario, a back-end clinical definition  is converted to a front-end study definition  by mapper server module  (FIG. ). In the second use case scenario, server process module  and\/or data exchange module  obtains clinical data from front-end sites  and, using the appropriate conversion map  as a translation key, formats the clinical data in manner that can be stored by O\/C clinical module  in database  in accordance with a back-end clinical definition . In the third use case scenario, data validation module  () detects a discrepancy and works with server process module  to send the discrepancy to the correct front-end site  for resolution.",{"@attributes":{"id":"p-0129","num":"0152"},"figref":["FIG. 6","FIG. 6"],"b":["8","70","602","8","10","8","10","12"]},"In processing step , a metatable of the back-end clinical definition  is selected. For example, consider the case in which the back-end clinical definition  is an Oracle Clinical definition having metatables described in Table 3. The goal of the processing steps depicted in , then, is to use as much of the information provided in the metatables of the Oracle Clinical definition to construct metatables in a front-end study definition  so that RDE product  will query for clinical data with data entry forms that resemble data entry forms of the Oracle Clinical definition in accordance with a schedule that resembles the schedule used to present the forms of the Oracle Clinical definition. Thus, in the case where the back-end clinical definition  is an Oracle Clinical definition, processing step  may select a metatable of the Oracle Clinical definition such as CLINICAL_PLANNED_EVENT, CLINICAL_STUDY, DATA_COLLECTION_INSTRUMENT (DCI), and so forth. Generally speaking, processing steps  through  will then mine as much information out of the selected metatable to construct a front-end study definition  that adheres to the clinical protocol defined in the Oracle Clinical definition.","For each back-end clinical definition  selected in processing step , a corresponding front-end study definition  and conversion map  is created. The front-end study definition  includes a set of metatables, such as the metatables found in Table 2. The definition and format of the metatables in the front-end study definition  are determined by the specific RDE product  used by front-end site . Representative RDE products that may be used to create a front-end study definition  are provided by vendors such as Infermed, Ltd., (London, UK), Phase Forward Inc., (Waltham, Mass.), CB Technology, (Philadelphia, Pa.), TEAMworks, (Hannover, Germany), DataTRAK, (Cleveland, Ohio), and Araccel, (Stockholm Sweden). When the RDE product  is MACRO (Infermed, Ltd.), the front-end study definition  has the metatables defined in Table 2.","In processing step , a determination is made as to whether any of the metatables in the front-end study definition  could use information found in the metatable selected in processing step . If the information could be used (-Yes), control passes to processing step . If the information could not possibly be used in the front-end study definition , (-No), control passes to processing step .","In processing step , the data found in the metatable selected in processing step  is formatted in accordance with a format required by the corresponding front-end study definition . What follows are exemplary actions taken by processing step  in the case in which the back-end clinical definition  is an Oracle Clinical definition and the front-end study definition  is a macro study definition. When the metatable selected in processing step  is the CLINICAL_PLANNED_EVENT metatable in an Oracle Clinical definition (Table 3), processing step  extracts the name of the clinical trial from the CLINICAL_PLANNED_EVENT metatable and places the name of the clinical trial in the ClinicalTrial metatable of the macro study definition (Table 2). Similarly, clinical trial header information found in the CLINICAL_STUDY metatable of the Oracle Clinical definition (Table 3) is extracted and placed in the StudyDefinition metatable of the macro study definition (Table 2). A more complex case is presented when processing step  selects a DCI metatable of the Oracle Clinical definition (Table 3). The DCI metatable is a series of clinical questions presented to a data entrant on an electronic form. The metatable includes not only the questions, but their position on an 80\u00d740 character based display. In this case, processing step  extracts the questions from the DCI and uses the extracted questions to construct a Dataltem metatable in the macro study definition. In another example, Oracle Clinical definition metatables DISCRETE_VALUE and DISCRETE_VALUE_GROUPSs (Table 3) correspond roughly to macro study definition metatables ValueData (Table 2). Accordingly, the correspondence between Oracle Clinical DISCRETE_VALUE and DISCRETE_VALUE_GROUP metatables, and macro study definition ValueData metatables is used in processing step  to populate ValueData metatables in the macro study definition.","In processing step , the reformatted data generated during processing step  is stored in the appropriate metatable of the front-end study definition . Finally, a record of the data is stored in the corresponding conversion map  in processing step .","If there is no metatable in the front-end study definition  that could use data found in the metatable selected during processing step , (-No), a record of the data in the metatable is stored in the corresponding conversion map  in processing step  or discarded. In one embodiment, the back-end study definition  defines the position of clinical questions on an 80\u00d740 character-based display. For example, the back-end clinical definition may have VTI100 codes that designate where a question will appear on a text-based screen. Furthermore, the back-end clinical definition may designate graphic characters to be displayed on an 80\u00d740 character-based legacy display during data entry. Such graphics may be characters for horizontal or vertical lines that are found in the VTI100 extended character set. In the case where the back-end clinical definition  is an Oracle Clinical definition, such graphics are stored in the DCM_LAYOUT_GRAPHIC metatable (Table 3). When processing step  selects a DCM_LAYOUT_GRAPHIC metatable, the condition -No is satisfied () and, in fact, the contents of DCM_LAYOUT_GRAPHIC are ignored because the eCRF form of the macro study definition uses far more sophisticated graphics. Another example of a situation in which -No arises is in the case where an Oracle Clinical definition defines the number of times a question will be repeated. Macro study definitions do not have repeat question functionality, and thus cannot make use of the Oracle Clinical definition attribute.","After processing step  has been executed, a determination  is made as to whether there are any other metatables in back-end clinical definition  that have not been selected by an instance of processing step . If so (-Yes), control returns to processing step  where a metatable of back-end clinical definition , which has not been selected by a previous instance of processing step , is selected. If there are no remaining metatables of back-end clinical definition  to process, (-No), control passes to processing step  where the front-end study definition  is published on each front-end site  used to collect clinical data for the clinical study defined by the back-end clinical definition  selected in processing step . Then, in processing step , the conversion map , which is defined by the sequential execution of processing step  in the manner shown in , is stored in database module  on computer . In processing step  the process ends.","Reference will now be made to , which disclose selected data segments that are found in conversion maps  in embodiments of the invention in which the back-end clinical definition is an Oracle Clinical definition (Table 3) and the front-end study definition  is a macro study definition. A conversion map  is used during \u201cUse Case 1\u201d, \u201cUse Case 2\u201d, and \u201cUse Case 3.\u201d In \u201cUse Case 1,\u201d symbolic links are built for the components of front-end study definition  that are equivalent or analogous to the components of the corresponding back-end clinical definition . In \u201cUse Case 2,\u201d where clinical data is collected from front-end sites , the conversion map  is used to store data about clinicians, clinical sites  enrolled in a clinical trial, and patient data. Then, the symbolic links created in processing step  of \u201cUse Case 1\u201d are used to construct a back-end data packet that has the clinician\/clinical site \/patient data obtained during \u201cUse Case 2.\u201d The back-end data packet is then imported into O\/C database . The data segments of conversion map  that are appended during \u201cUse Case 2,\u201d () will be described in the section entitled \u201cUse Case 2.\u201d","For each CLINICAL_PLANNED_EVENT metatable in an Oracle Clinical definition (Table 3), mapper server module  creates a corresponding StudyVisit metatable in the macro study definition (Table 2) and adds a record of this correspondence to segment  (FIG. A). In segment , the first column is a single-field look-up key to a component of an eCRF form found in a macro study definition. Column two in segment  is a single-field look-up key to a DCI metatable of the corresponding Oracle Clinical definition. Column  in segment  is the reference identifier for a DCM metatable (Table 3) in the Oracle Clinical definition. Like columns , and , columns - identify various components of an Oracle Clinical definition.","Now that the data structure of segment  has been defined, the advantages of segment  may be described. Referring to the first data row of segment , when server process module  receives code , it knows that an entry has been made to component  of an eCRF associated with the front-end study definition. The entry to component  of an eCRF could be, for example, the name of a patient. Furthermore, because of the symbolic information found in segment , server process module  knows that the response to component  of the macro eCRF form should be entered into the DCI metatable  of the corresponding back-end Oracle Clinical definition.","As noted in Table 3, an Oracle Clinical definition includes one or more data collection instruments (DCIs). When a DCI metatable is selected in processing step , mapper server module  places components of the DCI into two segments of conversion map , an OcDci segment (, element ) and an OcDciMod segment (, element ). The OcDci and OcDciMod segments serve the function of collecting information that correlates a DCI metatable (Table 3) of an Oracle Clinical definition with corresponding elements in an eCRF form within a macro study definition. Thus, the first column in segment  contains two numbers separated by a period delimiter. The first number represents a particular eCRF form within the macro study definition. The second number represents a particular component, such as a clinical question, in the designated eCRF form. While the first column of segment  () references a component of the macro study definition, remaining columns in segment  reference various aspects associated with a DCI metatable of an Oracle Clinical definition.","Now that the structure of segment  has been disclosed, an example of how the segment is used by server process module  can be described. When server process module  receives data associated with tmMapKey ., it knows that the data is a clinical response to component  of eCRF form . The exact nature of the data associated with tmMapKey . is dependent upon the nature of component . of the macro study definition. For example, component . could be the question \u201cGender?\u201d on eCRF form  and the data associated with tmMapKey . could therefore be the answer to this question, i.e. \u201cMale\u201d or \u201cFemale.\u201d When server process module  () receives the data associated with tmMapKey ., it performs a table lookup in segment  and knows that the data associated with tmMapKey . should be routed to the DCI metatable  of the corresponding Oracle Clinical definition.","In , exemplary OcDciMod segment  is listed with each row converted to a column for clarity. Thus, the first column represents the names of the elements within segment  whereas columns  and  represent two rows of data from a conversion map  used in an actual clinical study. OcDciMod segment  maps groups of questions found on an eCRF page-in a macro study definition to groups of questions found in an Oracle Clinical definition. For example, the first column of data in segment  () references the group of questions \u201c317.null.\u201d That is, the TmMapKey identifier references any question in the 317 group, such as 317.1 (question ), 317.2 (question ), and so forth. Next, segment  states that the group of question having the TmMapKey  in the macro study definition is equivalent to the DCM (Table 3) having an id of 32936. Thus, whenever server process module  receives data associated with a TmMapKey identifier 317.null, it knows that the data is associated with a group of questions within the macro study definition  and that the responses to these questions will need to be placed in the DCM group .","Taken together, segments  and  show one advantage of the present invention. By independently storing a symbolic link that traces the relationship of an individual clinical question in a back-end clinical definition  to a front-end study , the question can be modified at a later date without editing the group in which the question belongs.","The DCM metatables of an Oracle Clinical definition (Table 3) are stored in the OcQuestion segment  () of conversion map . As noted above, an Oracle Clinical DCM metatable includes a group of data collection instruments (DCIs), such as clinical questions.","Questions from an Oracle Clinical DCM have attributes that are not found in corresponding macro study definition metatables. For example, a DCM may have attributes that indicate that a clinical question be repeatedly asked until the user no longer provides information. An example of the use of this \u201crepeat\u201d attribute is the case in which the prompt \u201cPlease list another medication that is being taken by the patient\u201d is repeated until the data entrant no longer provides another medication taken by the patient. While Oracle Clinical definitions have the \u201crepeat\u201d attribute, macro study definitions do not. Consequently, the \u201crepeat\u201d attribute found in the back-end clinical definition is stored in segment  (FIG. B). Segment  also stores questions or attributes from front-end study definition  that are wholly derived from other front-end metatables and therefore do not correspond to back-end metatables.","Laboratory ranges. In some embodiments of the present invention, discrepancies, lab values, coded values, and ranges are translated from a back-end clinical definition  to a front-end study definition , in addition to the metatable data described above. Such information includes code values for sites and corresponding investigators as well as patients that are participating in a clinical trial. Ranges includes laboratory normal ranges (e.g., upper and lower limits on serum hemoglobin concentration for healthy men and women). In such embodiments, the results of the process described in  is the creation of a front-end study definition  that includes question attributes, form layout, form order, and visit scheduling that is defined by a back-end clinical definition .","Thesaurus loaded questions. In some embodiments, the generated front-end study definition  will include, as not enterable, questions designated as thesaurus-coded questions. In one embodiment, the back-end clinical definition  will indicate that a question is a thesaurus-coded question by assigning to it a zero-length discrete value group (e.g., a code list). The corresponding question in the front-end study definition will not be enterable by a clinician.","Centrally loaded question. In some embodiments, the generated front-end study definition  will include, as not enterable, questions, question groups, and data collection modules designated as centrally loaded questions. For example, laboratory questions may be designated as centrally loaded questions in the back-end clinical definition . Then, in the corresponding front-end study definition , the question will be designated as not enterable.","Form format. In some embodiments of the present invention, forms in the front-end study definition  will be formatted in a manner that duplicates the layout defined for data-entry screens in back-end clinical definition , within the spatial limits imposed RDE product  (FIG. ).","Updating a front-end study definition  based on a back-end clinical definition . In some embodiments of the present invention, a front-end study definition  can be updated based on modification made to a back-end clinical definition. Such updates can be performed either before or after a clinical study has been initiated using the front-end study definition . Typically, such updates are in the form of additions. In one example, additions are made to the back-end clinical definition  and the additions are propagated to each corresponding front-end study definition  using methods such as those disclosed in FIG. . When updating a front-end study definition, restriction imposed by O\/C clinical module  and RDE product  on updates to deployed studies are not violated. Furthermore, when allowed by RDE product  and O\/C clinical module , the methods of the present invention can be used to implement question-modification changes, including field-length changes, code-list changes, and data type changes.","Performing study audits. In some embodiments of the present invention, automatic audits of corresponding back-end clinical definitions  and front-end study definitions  are performed to detect incompatibilities that would prevent successful translation and transferal of any user responses to study questions. In one embodiment, derived questions, questions and forms may be added to front-end study definition  and designated as nonclinical. Responses to the derived questions, questions, and forms that are designated as nonclinical are not transferred to the CDMS because the corresponding back-end clinical definition  does not include derived questions, questions and forms that are designated as nonclinical. Rather, the answers to these derived questions are audited using, for example, database module  and audit trail .",{"@attributes":{"id":"p-0152","num":"0175"},"figref":["FIG. 11","FIG. 11"],"b":["104","12","1300","1","1102","38","40","40","1300","1","40","104","40"]},"In processing step , the name of one of the clinical trials  tracked by system  is retrieved from configuration file . Then, in processing step , one of the front-end sites  presently collecting data for the clinical trial, \u201cactive clinical trial X,\u201d is obtained. In processing step , the identity of \u201cactive clinical trial X\u201d and the front-end site  is used to poll a time stamp  that corresponds to front-end site  in the status account book  of persistent state record  (FIG. ). In principle, there exists a stamp  that corresponds to each clinical trial that is being conducted at a front-end site  in system . The time stamp  represents the date and time at which a query for clinical data from front-end site  was last made by server process module . After a front-end site  has been queried for clinical data, the corresponding time stamp  is set to the current date and time.","In processing step , database  of front-end site  is polled to determine whether any clinical data has been acquired since the time stamp , corresponding to the clinical trial retrieved in processing step , was last set. If data has been acquired at front-end site  since time stamp  was set (-Yes), then processing steps  through  are performed. If data has not been acquired since time stamp  was set (-No), control passes to processing step  where configuration file  is checked to determine whether there exists any additional front-end sites  within system  that are collecting data for the \u201cactive clinical trial X\u201d retrieved in processing step .","When new data is available in database  at front-end site  (-Yes), the data is packaged into a front-end data packet and sent to the server hosting server process module  (processing step ). The front-end data packet is formatted in accordance with the particular front-end study definition  that is associated with the \u201cactive clinical trial X\u201d retrieved in processing step .","In processing step , the front-end data packet retrieved in processing step  is parsed by obtaining the name of a new patient in the front-end data packet. As used herein, a new patient is defined as one that has not been mapped in the conversion map , corresponding to a given front-end study definition , to the O\/C identifiers  (FIG. ), describing a corresponding O\/C site, O\/C investigator, and O\/C patient code.","In processing step , server process module  looks for responses in the front-end data packet to special questions set up in the required identifier form of the front-end study definition . In processing step , if these O\/C identifier questions are properly filled in the front-end data packet (-Yes), then server process module  adds the new patient to the conversion map  that corresponds to \u201cactive clinical study X\u201d and the front-end study definition . It will be appreciated that the new patient is added to the conversion map  in such a manner that the patient can be tracked in either the front-end study definition  or the corresponding back-end clinical definition .","When any new patient lacks one or more of the requisite front-end site , investigator or patient code designations required by O\/C identifiers  (-No), server process module  notes the error and notifies the operator of front-end site  in processing step . Furthermore, all clinical data from that front-end site  is postponed until appropriate O\/C identifiers  have been entered for all patients. In other embodiments of the present invention, the new patient data is rejected in processing step . A query is then made for additional new patients in the front-end data packet. When additional patients exist in the front-end data packet (-Yes), processing step  is repeated.","When there are no additional patients in the front-end data packet (-No), the conversion map  corresponding to the clinical trial is used to construct a back-end data packet, one data record at a time in processing step . The resulting O\/C sequence of responses may differ in length from the corresponding sequence stored in database . For example, in one embodiment of the present invention, repeat defaults in Oracle Clinical definitions are not even questions in macro study definitions, so server process module  creates an Oracle Clinical definition defaulted response where no such audit-trail record exists in the corresponding macro study definition. As another example, certain required-identifier questions are special questions created by exemplary server process module  for the macro study definition during \u201cUse Case 1.\u201d Therefore, they do not exist in Oracle Clinical definitions. For any response to such questions, there will not be corresponding rows in the back-end data packet. However, in a preferred embodiment of the present invention, all responses provided by RDE product  appear in the same order in the back-end data packet. Once the back-end data packet has been generated, it is uploaded into O\/C database  using O\/C data capture API .","After processing step , control passes to processing step  where configuration file  is checked to determine whether there exists any additional front-end sites  within system  that are collecting data for the \u201cactive clinical trial X\u201d retrieved in processing step . If there are additional front-end sites  that are collecting clinical data for \u201cactive clinical trial X\u201d (-Yes), control returns to processing step , where a different front-end site  that is collecting data for \u201cactive clinical trial X\u201d is selected. If configuration file  reveals that there are no additional front-end sites  presently collecting clinical data for \u201cactive clinical trial X\u201d (-No), then control passes to processing step .","In processing step , a query of configuration file  is made to determine whether there are any additional clinical trials presently being tracked by system . If there are (-Yes), control returns to processing step , where a different active \u201cclinical trial X\u201d is retrieved from configuration file , and processing steps  through  are repeated accordingly. The process ends () if there are no additional clinical trials presently being tracked by system  (-No).","In typical embodiments, the exemplary processing steps shown in  are performed in accordance with a schedule. For example, in one embodiment, processing step  is initiated on a daily basis using an automated scheduler.","Now that the processing steps in  have been disclosed, segments of conversion map  updated during \u201cUse Case 2\u201d may be described. Generally speaking segment  () maps clinical sites from the front-end study definition to the corresponding back-end clinical definition, segment A () maps the identity of investigators collecting clinical data from the front-end study definition to the back-end clinical definition, and segment  () maps actual patients from the front-end study definition to the back-end clinical definition.","Segment  () depicts an OcSite segment  that is found within some exemplary conversion maps . The segment  collects information from front-end sites . In column  of segment , the tmMapKey refers to patients enrolled in front-end site \u201crp101621.\u201d Accordingly, the first data row in segment  references patient number  at front-end site  \u201crp101621,\u201d the second row refers to patient  at site \u201crp101621,\u201d and the third row references patient  at site \u201crp101621.\u201d Columns  through  list the corresponding Oracle Clinical definition identifier information for the site information found in column . Segment  is used to route any information associated with a given front-end site  to the unique components of the back-end clinical definition that are reserved for that site.","Segment  () tracks the names of investigators that are collecting data for each patient at front-end sites . Column  references the site and patient id. For example, in the first data row of segment , patient  at site \u201crp101621\u201d is listed. Column  discloses the id of the investigator that is collecting data for the patient. Column  discloses the Oracle Clinical id of the investigator that is collecting data for the patient disclosed in column . Segment  is used to route any information associated with a given clinical investigator at a front-end site  to the unique components of the back-end clinical definition that are reserved for that clinical investigator.","Segment  () depicts an exemplary OcPatient segment  that is found within some conversion maps  in accordance with the present invention. Segment  of conversion maps  collects patient identifier information available from the front-end study definition  required identifiers form, which mapper server module  creates for the front-end study definition . Segment  is used to route any information associated with a given patient at a front-end site  to the unique components of the back-end clinical definition that are reserved for that patient.","Segment  () depicts an exemplary OcKey segment  that is found within some conversion maps . The OcKey records one-to-one correlations between some metatables of an Oracle Clinical definition and corresponding metatables of the macro study definition that were generated in the processing steps of \u201cUse Case 1.\u201d Such correlations include correspondences between DISCRETE VALUE metatables of an Oracle Clinical definition (Table 3) and corresponding ValueData metatables of the macro study definition (Table 2).","Segment  () depicts an exemplary SpecialValues segment  that is found within some conversion maps . In particular, segment  shows the values used in a representative clinical trial. The SpecialValues segment records identifies the data items that provide information that data exchange module  must use to correlate a front-end site  and patient identifiers with O\/C clinical module , investigator and patient identifiers. Column  of segment  provides visit identifiers and data item identifiers for front-end study definition .","Error Handling. Because server process module  interacts with a number of different modules that are potentially distributed across several different servers and desktop computers throughout system  (FIG. ), a preferred embodiment of server process module  includes a robust error handling feature set. The following is a set of representative error handling features provided in some embodiments of the present invention.","Broken connection\/loss of system service: Connection problems to either RDE product  via data exchange module  or O\/C clinical module  result in server process module  informing the administrator user by E-mail, then retrying the connection until it is restored.","Data errors\u2014disabled sites: In some embodiments of the present invention, when an error is detected with the data retrieved from RDE product  (, processing step ) or during loading of that data into O\/C database  (, processing step ) the front-end site  from which the data came will be marked as \u201cbad\u201d causing further loads of data from that front-end site  to be disabled until the problem is corrected. Once the problem is resolved, the front-end site  is reenabled using the console module  and processing is enabled for front-end site .","Front-end sites  postponed for incomplete O\/C identifiers: For any translation or data-loading error, server process module  marks the originating front-end site  as problematic in some embodiments of the present invention. Once marked as problematic, exemplary server process module  will not translate or load data from the front-end site  until the problem is rectified. In cases of translation or loading error, the fix will depend on the administrator. Once exemplary server process module  finds O\/C identifiers  to fix the original patient-mapping problem, module  requests all data from RDE product  resident on front-end site  since before the original problem arose. Accordingly, in one embodiment of the present invention, status account book  in database module  keeps two time stamps per site: one for the last successfully loaded macro response, and one for the most recent time stamp for the front-end site  at which time O\/C identifiers  were still missing for a patient. In some embodiments, data from a front-end site is not postponed when there is a problem with data from an individual patient. Rather, server process module  refuses to process data for that patient until the problem with the patient data is resolved.","Internal errors: Exemplary server process module  records a persistent log of all events that occur in persistent state record  (FIG. ). Events considered as fatal errors, such as those that cause system malfunction, are trapped where possible and cause an alarm E-mail to be sent to the administration user.","Incremental transfer of response data: In some embodiments of the present invention, database module  will maintain status account information for clinical data, tracking what data and discrepancies are new. Further, status-account information will be maintained on a per-patient basis for each patient in a clinical trial. In one embodiment of the present invention, the audit trail for RDE product  will be polled for visit-date changes and will apply these visit-date changes to applicable data collection instruments and data collection modules in the corresponding back-end clinical definition .","Transfer of laboratory data and coded thesaurus terms: In some embodiments of the present invention, laboratory data and coded thesaurus terms are translated from O\/C database  to RDE product . Laboratory data is typically obtained in a manner that is independent of front-end sites . For example, in some embodiments, laboratory results are loaded into O\/C database  from a laboratory using a generic loader . In one embodiment, data that is designated laboratory data or as a code thesaurus term is not reloaded from the front-end  to O\/C database .","1. Introduction. The present invention provides a novel form of packet structure that is used to exchange data between RDE product  and O\/C database  using conversion map  in accordance with one embodiment of the present invention (FIG. ). In one embodiment, back-end clinical definition  is an Oracle clinical definition and front-end study definition  is a macro study definition. However, those of skill in the art will appreciate that the packets of the present invention may be used for types of back-end clinical definitions  other than the Oracle clinical definition as well as for types of front-end study definitions other than a Macro study definition. Such packets would be similar to those disclosed herein.","The data packets are suitable for system  where data exchange that is insulated from the data structure requirements of a back-end CDMS and a front-end RDE is desired. An exemplary case is the situation in which the back-end CDMS uses a clinical definition  that is an Oracle clinical definition and the front-end RDE uses a study definition  that is a macro study definition. Clinical definition  and study definition  are not identical in format although they encompass the same clinical trial data. The data packets of the present invention can be used to exchange data between these two formats.","Data packets in accordance with one embodiment of the present invention provide a generic \u201cpacket\u201d data structure that encapsulates data that is in either Oracle Clinical or MACRO format. In one embodiment of the present invention, back-end packets and front-end packets described in \u201cUse Case 1\u201d and \u201cUse Case 2\u201d have a similar data structure. In addition to site, clinician, and patient data, such packets include support for collections of data that are used for accounting purposes and for the mapping relationship between the front-end study definition  and the corresponding back-end clinical definition .","The advantage of using a \u201cpacket\u201d that is formatted in a back-end and front-end independent data structure is that code mechanisms that handle the packets at a generic level can be re-used rather than having to code for each specific back-end or front-end product. For example, in one embodiment, the packets of the instant invention provide a mechanism that allows for storage of any \u201cpacket\u201d in a persistent data store.","Another advantage of data packets in accordance with this embodiment of the present invention is that the contents of the packet are easily modified without having to re-compile source code because the packet definition is held in a file that is independent of the front-end or back-end. This definition in itself is useful as it allows for standardization of the contents of a packet as well as the management of different versions of the system.","2. General packet data structure. The data structure of a packet in accordance with one embodiment of the present invention is illustrated in FIG. . Packet , which is formatted in a back-end or front-end independent data structure, has the following basic structure:\n\n","(i) Packet header . The packet header portion of the packet allows for the recordation of the type of data contained in the packet (e.g., data type ) along with audit trail information , such as the system version and who created or modified the packet. The header values are stored as a series of properties so that they can be extended without the need to recompile the existing code base. processing step , the TM Meta packet is delivered to RDE product . In processing step , the RDE product is instructed to convert the TM Meta Packet into a front-end study definition. In some embodiments, processing step  is facilitated using an application programming interface  that is provided by the RDE product . The use of an application programming interface (\u201cAPI\u201d )  is advantageous because it allows for the upload of a front-end study definition  into an RDE product  without any knowledge of the specific architecture of RDE product . Products such as MACRO 3.0 include an API .","Once the TM Meta packet corresponding to the clinical trial \u201cBA15428\u201d is delivered to RDE product  at a site , the site  can commence collecting clinical data for trial \u201cBA15428.\u201d At a later date, therefore, the clinical data collected at site  is collected from front-end site  and transferred to back-end site . In one embodiment of the present invention, packets  are used to perform this task, using the processing steps illustrated in FIG. .","In step , RDE product  is instructed to poll database  for new data for a given clinical trial that is managed by the front-end study definition  that corresponds to the clinical trial \u201cBA15428.\u201d In some embodiments, API  facilitates step . When data is found, process control passes to step . In step , RDE product  is instructed to format available clinical data for clinical trial \u201cBA15428\u201d into a \u201cTM Data Packet.\u201d The TM Data Packet has the data structure illustrated in , including a packet header  and data segments . packets having the novel data structure disclosed in  can be used to export back-end clinical definitions from a CDMS to a front-end RDE as well as to send data from the RDE to a back-end CDMS in accordance with \u201cUse Case 1\u201d and \u201cUse Case 2.\u201d","One advantage of the present invention is the manner in which discrepancies are resolved. Discrepancies arise in a number of different situations. For example, a discrepancy arises when clinical data has been entered that is not consistent with allowed data types and\/or data ranges. In some embodiments of the present invention, a discrepancy is identified by data validation module  (FIG. ). The steps in which a discrepancy is discovered and resolved in accordance with one embodiment are illustrated in  in conjunction with system  (FIG. ).","In step  (FIG. ), data validation module  detects a discrepancy in O\/C database . Data validation module  () is a component of O\/C clinical module  in accordance with some embodiments of the present invention. It will be appreciated that a discrepancy may be discovered in O\/C database  using other modules, such as modules that are not shown in  or  discrepancy is any form of data entry that is inconsistent with the clinical design. For example, a discrepancy is a data value that exceeds an allowed data range. In the case of a blood pressure measurement, a discrepancy is a nonsensical measurement, such as \u201c10\u201d over \u201c20.\u201d Because data validation module  has access to the data collected for every subject in a clinical trial, discovery of more complex discrepancies is possible. For example, data validation module  may determine that the estrogen levels in a particular male subject, or group of male subjects, is higher than any other male subjects surveyed. Therefore, although the measured estrogen levels are within allowed ranges, data validation module  may flag the systematic high estrogen level as a discrepancy.","Referring to step , server process module  is notified of the discrepancy. In response, server process module  retrieves the clinical trial X in which the discrepancy arose from configuration file  (FIG. ). One of skill in the art will appreciate that there is a substantial number of different ways in which step  may be performed. For example, in some embodiments, server process module  is always running and the data for clinical trial X is already loaded. In step , the front-end site  where the discrepancy arose is identified using configuration file  (FIG. ). An important aspect of \u201cUse Case 3\u201d is that the discrepancy resolution is performed in a manner that is fully audited in accordance with regulatory agency guidelines. Accordingly, in step , audit trail  () is updated to note the discrepancy that was discovered by data validation module  in O\/C database . In some embodiments, step  comprises updating an audit trail (not shown) for the back-end CDMS  () and an audit trail (not shown) for the front-end RDE system  (FIG. ). In some embodiments of the present invention, step  is performed in conjunction with audit trail module  () and\/or database module .","An advantage of the present invention is that data that is stored in accordance with a back-end clinical definition may be communicated to a front-end site  Furthermore, data collected at a front-end site  may be communicated to a back-end CDMS, such as computer . Because the back-end and front-end sites use very different data formats, a conversion step is used. Accordingly, in process step , the discrepancy is converted from the back-end format used to store the clinical value or values associated with the discrepancy into a form that is compatible with the appropriate front-end study definition . Conversion step  takes advantage of the novel conversion map  described above. Conversion map  includes a record of matching first and second components in the back-end clinical definition  and the corresponding front-end study definition  (FIG. ).","In processing step , the discrepancy is sent to the front-end site  where the discrepancy was entered. Typically, step  involves sending the discrepancy to RDE product  where it is interpreted in conjunction with the front-end study definition  that corresponds to the clinical study in which the discrepancy arose. In one embodiment of the present invention, the discrepancy is sent to RDE product  with a message generated by data validation module . For example, the data validation module  may state the nature of the discrepancy and any appropriate responses. In one instance, the observed clinical event in which a discrepancy arose may be a query that asks whether the subject has a cough. In response, the clinician responded \u201cnot determined.\u201d Data validation module  notes a discrepancy and sends, along with the discrepancy (e.g., the data value that must be reentered correctly) a message stating \u201cYes\/No answer required.\u201d","In processing step , server process module  and\/or data exchange module  receives the discrepancy response from RDE product . In step , the discrepancy response is then stored in audit trail  and in step  the discrepancy response is converted into the appropriate back-end clinical definition format  using the appropriate conversion map . Then, the discrepancy response is transferred to back-end computer  (FIG. ). It will be appreciated that the temporal sequence of many of the steps disclosed above, including steps  and  is not important. In step , data validation module  determines whether the response received from RDE  resolves the discrepancy. If so (; -Yes), then the discrepancy response is stored as a discrepancy resolution in O\/C database . Further, the back-end discrepancy is closed. In the example where a \u201cYes\u201d or \u201cNo\u201d answer was required, the discrepancy response may be the answer \u201cYes.\u201d Because the answer \u201cYes\u201d is an allowed answer to the query, data validation module  accepts the answer and replaces the previous value (e.g., \u201cnot determined\u201d) with the value \u201cYes\u201d in step . In instances where the response does not resolve the discrepancy (; -No), this failure is noted in audit trail  in step . Then, process control returns to step , in which the discrepancy is sent to the front-end site  where the discrepancy was entered for further resolution.","The process disclosed in  is advantageous for a number of reasons. Rather than sending a FAX, letter or report when a data validation module  discovers a discrepancy, the present invention makes use of the novel conversion map  to query a front-end site directly about the discrepancy. Then, the conversion map  is again utilized to convert the discrepancy response and, if acceptable, store the response in the CDMS (e.g., back-end site ). Furthermore, the process disclosed in  is advantageous because the electronic audit measures found in system  () may automatically be used without manual input. Yet another advantage of the process disclosed in  is that it is performed in a paperless fashion. Thus, the process disclosed in  resolves discrepancies in a fully automated, audited fashion, with minimal reliance on manual input.","Using Packets to resolve discrepancies. In one embodiment of the present invention, \u201cUse Case 3\u201d is facilitated by the use of packets having the data structure disclosed in FIG. . This embodiment is illustrated in FIG. . The steps illustrated in  may be used to execute the embodiment shown in FIG. . In step , O\/C clinical module  discovers a discrepancy in O\/C database  and packetizes (formats) the discrepancy into an O\/C Discrepancy Packet that has the data structure disclosed in FIG. . In processing step , the O\/C Discrepancy Packet is transferred to computer . In processing step , mapper server module  (FIG. ), working in conjunction with data exchange module  and mapper server module , converts the O\/C Discrepancy Packet into a front-end TM Discrepancy Packet. The front-end TM Discrepancy Packet has the data structure disclosed in FIG. . In step , the TM Discrepancy Packet is transferred to RDE product  on site . In step , an investigator corrects the discrepancy. Subsequently, the resolved discrepancy may be transferred back to O\/C database in a manner that reverses the steps illustrated in FIG. . Alteratively, the resolved discrepancy can be transferred to O\/C database  using the processing steps illustrated in FIG. .","Patient Registration. When allowed by RDE product , and for those studies that allow site-initiated patient enrollment, one embodiment of the present invention will allow a front-end study definition  to be configured to avoid reliance on manually-entered patient, investigator, and site codes. In studies where automatic assignment of patient codes is not feasible, one embodiment of the present invention will require identifier-code responses (derived or manually entered) prior to loading data for that subject using O\/C clinical module . Where the identifier-code response is missing or inappropriate (e.g., wrong patient code for the designated site and investigator), one embodiment of the present invention will not load that patient's data until the code is corrected. However, other patient data from that site will continue loading. If an OC database  patient code is already associated with a subject of front-end study definition , one embodiment of the present invention will reject that patient code as an assignment for a different patient at the same site .\n\nCompatibility. Some embodiments of the present invention operate with Oracle Clinical version 4.0 and MACRO version 3. Some embodiments of the present invention operate with Oracle Clinical version 4.0 and MACRO version 2 installations. Some embodiments of the present invention operate with Oracle Clinical version 3.1.1.1 and MACRO version 3. Some embodiments of the present invention operate with Oracle Clinical version 3.1.1.1 and MACRO version 2 installations. Some embodiments of the present invention work with MACRO v2.2.\n\nActivity and Error Logs. Some embodiments of the present invention include activity and error logs at different levels of granularity. The events that are recorded by such error logs include, for example, user actions, such as metadata mapping, re-configuration, study audits, and administrative pausing and restarting of activity for individual sites or studies. In some embodiments, such logs will record successful and unsuccessful executions of data-translation and data-loading steps.\n\nSecurity. In some embodiments of the present invention, all remote users (e.g., user of console module , users of mapper server module , and users of server process module ) have access to an external, corporate user directory (e.g., via lightweight directory access protocol). Furthermore, in some embodiments of the present invention, the system administrator is permitted to either store database-account passwords or to require that users enter them manually whenever system  is initiated.\n\nHadValue. Some embodiments of the present invention work with MACRO version 2.2. In particular, some embodiments use the MACRO 2.2 HadValue field to detect that deletion of a value with a skip-condition has occurred. In such instances, such deletions (e.g., the start and end dates of a deleted medication) will be transferred to O\/C database  from RDE .\n\nRepeating groups. Some embodiments of the present invention allow back-end clinical definition  designers to update a repeating group to have a new, higher maximum number of repeats.\n\nStudy audits. In some embodiments, mandatory questions that are not in any data collection instrument book page (Table 3) in a back-end clinical definition  are ignored. That is, such question are not placed in the corresponding front-end study definition  that is created using the conversion algorithms of the present invention.\n","All references cited herein are incorporated by reference in their entirety and for all purposes to the same extent as if each individual publication or patent or patent application was specifically and individually indicated to be incorporated by reference in its entirety for all purposes.","The present invention can be implemented as a computer program product that comprises a computer program mechanism embedded in a computer readable storage medium.
